<div id="review_2467724950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2467724950" />
    <a title="Gumble&#39;s Yard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35482263-gumble-s-yard"><img alt="Gumble&#39;s Yard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604226927p2/35482263.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2467724950?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gumble&#39;s Yard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gumble&#39;s Yard" href="/user/show/35482263-gumble-s-yard">Gumble&#39;s Yard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785151637" href="/book/show/35661773-the-overstory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35482263-gumble-s-yard?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35482263-gumble-s-yard?shelf=2018-booker-shortlist">2018-booker-shortlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35482263-gumble-s-yard?shelf=pulitzer-prize-winning">pulitzer-prize-winning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35482263-gumble-s-yard?shelf=2018-booker-longlist">2018-booker-longlist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2467724950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3134623888309280759">As per the end of my review, the book has now deservedly won a medal but for lots of reasons (not least that the Booker really does not need another American based male author winning it) I hope it does not win the gold. <br/><br/>This book begins by giving the stories of a disparate group of individuals with different professions and backgrounds, and their interactions with the world of trees. <br/><br/>And so I would like to start my review by commending the reviews of a number of my Goodreads friends - a photogr</span>
  <span id="freeText3134623888309280759" style="display:none">As per the end of my review, the book has now deservedly won a medal but for lots of reasons (not least that the Booker really does not need another American based male author winning it) I hope it does not win the gold. <br /><br />This book begins by giving the stories of a disparate group of individuals with different professions and backgrounds, and their interactions with the world of trees. <br /><br />And so I would like to start my review by commending the reviews of a number of my Goodreads friends - a photographer with a passion for nature; an actuary (who unlike one character in the book actually qualified rather than taking drugs); and an ex music critic, now librarian and art blogger. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2162671066">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2261913637">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deucekindred.wordpress.com/2018/08/07/richard-powers-the-overstory/">https://deucekindred.wordpress.com/20...</a><br /><br />And then to add my own brief thoughts on a few other areas which I think are not captured in their reviews. <br /><br />The first is the concept of different timescales and in particular the link to Artificial intelligence; something which I think was vital to the very conception of this book which arose when the author was based around Silicon Valley but walking amongst ancient trees. <br /><br />The theme is first captured in a science fiction story that one character loved as a youngster (and later part remembers as an adult, albeit forgetting the ending). <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Aliens land on earth. They’re little runts, as alien races go. But they metabolise like there’s no tomorrow. They zip around like swarms of gnats, too fast to see - so fast that Earth seconds seem to them like tears. To them, humans are nothing but sculptures of immobile meat. The foreigners try to communicate, but there’s no reply. Finding no signs of intelligent life, they tuck unto the frozen statues and start curing them like so much jerky, for the long ride home.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The parallels with humans and trees are clear and later (in a related story) a character visiting an airport is drawn to the movements of birds rather than the static scene of departure boards - a symbol of how humankind is hardwired to focus in movement/change. <br /><br />Then as the first mentioned character starts to creates the artificial worlds in his MMORPGs and eventually diverges in his aims from those playing the games, and those around him in his old firm and, at the book’s end starts to use artificial intelligence for different purposes than those his game has been hijacked by, we see the dichotomy that Powers is exploring, one he has explained in early interviews. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Cultural transmission is orders of magnitude faster than genetic transmission, and digital transmission has accelerated the speed of culture a hundredfold or more. We may soon seem, to our artificial intelligence offspring, as motionless and insentient as trees seem to us. And here we live, trying to make a home between our predecessors and our descendants. Will we double down on the great migration into symbol space, our decampment into Facebook and Instagram and Netflix and World of Warcraft, the road that we have already traveled so far down? Or will Big Data and Deep Learning allow us to grasp and rejoin the staggeringly complex processes of the living world? The two possibilities are not mutually exclusive. Indeed, they’re inseparable aspects of the new ecology of digital life.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />A second theme is suicide. <br /><br />Of the characters whose individual stories start the novel and then interleaf throughout it: one’s father commits suicide; another contemplates it but is dissuaded by voices at the last moment; another makes an enfeebled attempt in hospital observed by a second character; another is thankful that the opportunity does not present itself in prison. And of course the book culminates with a lecture planned to end in suicide as advice on the best thing than a human can do to save the environment, before taking a late and different course. <br /><br />I saw two angles to this - firstly a view that the current obsession with consumption and new flirtations with climate change denial and rolling back environmental protections is itself a form of suicide; and secondly a counsel of hope against despair and that humans still have a role to play in serving the planet (what role does life want humans to play is of course the aim of the new Artificial intelligence established by the aforementioned character at the book’s end). <br /><br />Very much a book of ideas, if as has been pointed out in Paul’s review and the comments below it, ones that have largely been adopted from elsewhere and, slightly oddly, unattributed albeit Power himself seems to acknowledge that omission. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>The judges award him no medal - even a bronze. They say it’s because he has no bibliography. A bibliography is a required part of the formal report.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />A bibliography is not required for a novel but I think it would have been useful given the campaigning nature of the book, so I will add my own. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11468377.Thinking__Fast_and_Slow" title="Thinking, Fast and Slow by Daniel Kahneman" rel="nofollow noopener">Thinking, Fast and Slow</a> by the Nobel Prize winner <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/72401.Daniel_Kahneman" title="Daniel Kahneman" rel="nofollow noopener">Daniel Kahneman</a> is the definitive guide to the field of Behavioural Economics that underlies a lot of the book<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/475.Collapse_How_Societies_Choose_to_Fail_or_Succeed" title="Collapse How Societies Choose to Fail or Succeed by Jared Diamond" rel="nofollow noopener">Collapse: How Societies Choose to Fail or Succeed</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/256.Jared_Diamond" title="Jared Diamond" rel="nofollow noopener">Jared Diamond</a> is an excellent guide to societal suicide due to excessive growth outstripping resources and environmental degradation (including deforestation). <br /><br />Will the judges award this a medal - I would be very surprised and a little disappointed if it does not achieve the “bronze” of a shortlisting given the stimulating ideas it summarises; but equally not surprised and certainly not disappointed if it does not win the gold, not least due to comments in the book which in my view range somewhere on the spectrum of ignorant to insulting about my profession, industry and faith.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3134623888309280759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2464815219?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780393635522" href="/book/show/35187203-the-overstory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=ecopocalypse">ecopocalypse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=social-issues">social-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=hug-a-tree">hug-a-tree</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=best-of-2018">best-of-2018</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2464815219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5609822606626929847"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533311818i/26071520._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='275' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>"Thank you for the tools. The chests. The decking. The clothes closets. The paneling. I forget . . . Thank you," she says, following the ancient formula. "For all the gifts that you have given." And still not knowing how to stop, she adds, "We're sorry. We didn't know how hard it is for you to grow back."</b><br/><br/>Powers begins his monumental novel by introducing his characters - each with their own short story. Then, the characters begin to interact in a tale that is beautiful, heartbreaking, terrifying,</span>
  <span id="freeText5609822606626929847" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533311818i/26071520._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>"Thank you for the tools. The chests. The decking. The clothes closets. The paneling. I forget . . . Thank you," she says, following the ancient formula. "For all the gifts that you have given." And still not knowing how to stop, she adds, "We're sorry. We didn't know how hard it is for you to grow back."</b><br><br>Powers begins his monumental novel by introducing his characters - each with their own short story. Then, the characters begin to interact in a tale that is beautiful, heartbreaking, terrifying, and occasionally magical.<br><br><b>Out in the yard, all around the house, the things they've planted are making significance, making meaning, as easily as they make sugar and wood from nothing, from air, and sun, and rain. But the humans hear nothing.</b><br><br>This is an epic story about people and trees. There are clashes between loggers and protesters, and an act of eco-terrorism that has long reaching consequences. There are also dire warnings about the future as our growing population continues <b>using resources faster than the world can replace them</b>. As one character mentions, <b>"Demand for wood has tripled in our lifetime."</b> I didn't enjoy this part as much as the character introductions, but it still made for a powerful read.<br><br><b>"Trees stand at the heart of ecology, and they must come to stand at the heart of human politics. Tagore said, <i>Trees are the earth's endless effort to speak to the listening heaven.</i> But people ---oh, my word --- people! People could be the heaven that the Earth is trying to speak to.<br> <br>"If we could see green, we'd see a thing that keeps getting more interesting the closer we get. If we could see what green was doing, we'd never be lonely or bored. If we could understand green, we'd learn how to grow all the food we need in layers three deep, on a third of the ground we need right now, with plants that protected one another from pests and stress. If we know what green wanted, we wouldn't have to choose between the Earth's interests and ours. They'd be the same!"</b><br><br>This is one for the tree huggers, though it will make you very, very sad. <br>Thanks to W. W. Norton for the opportunity to read this unforgettable book.<br><br><b><i>People aren't the apex species they think they are.</i> Other creatures --- bigger, smaller, slower, faster, older, younger, more powerful --- call the shots, make the air, and eat sunlight. Without them, <i>nothing</i>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5609822606626929847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_55525261'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55525261-in-our-bones"><img alt="In Our Bones" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1601536135l/55525261._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KnnIhW3lnRrIQXfQbNOZ/iY5FT3jn+34a4IHipufFNvX0UFnc8nDzbn7Mg6ktY+hg8zL7M3JIMzgqAz5sUGSkw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p1J2n+mh2fWh11VwhvOeBH5vSiIEhkkR+x8iPF1XJ5da+v99942HItBtEK5OlYhb25qU8yrQhCVwNSlPd4mh3w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/11783.Richard_Powers">About Richard Powers</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/11783.Richard_Powers"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1263155076p3/11783.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/11783.Richard_Powers">Richard Powers
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,027
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3768783523727765911"><strong>Richard Powers</strong> is the author of twelve novels, most recently <em>The Overstory</em>. He is the recipient of a MacArthur Fellowship and the National Book Award, and he has been a Pulitzer Prize and four-time National Book Critics Circle Award finalist. He lives in the foothills of the Great Smoky Mountains.<br/><br/> <i>Librarian note: There is more than one author with this name in the Goodreads database. </i></span>

</div>
</div>
